Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Bhс╣Ыgu.тАФaс╣гс╣н─Бtriс╣Е┼Ыat. mantrokt─Бjam pa├▒c─Бudanadevatyam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 3. 4-p. puroti┼Ыakvar─л jagat─л; 4, 10. jagat─л; 14, 17, 27-30. anuс╣гс╣нubh (30. kakummat─л); 16. 3-p. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 18, 37. 3-p. vir─Бс╕Н g─Бjyatr─л; 23. purauс╣гс╣Зih; 24. 5-p. anuс╣гс╣нubuс╣гс╣Зiggarbho тАЩpariс╣гс╣н─Бdb─Бrhat─Б vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 20-22.?; 26. 5-p. anuс╣гс╣нubuс╣гс╣Зiggarbho тАЩpariс╣гс╣н─Бdb─Бrhat─Б bhurij; 31. 7-p. aс╣гс╣нi; 32-35. 10-p. prakс╣Ыti; 36. 10-p. ─Бkс╣Ыti; 38. 1-av. 2-p. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh.]

Whitney

Comment

тМКPartly proseтАФ“vss.” 16, 20-22, 31-36; also considerable parts of 23-30.тМЛ Found for the most part also in P─Бipp., but not all together, nor even all in the same book; the greater part of the vss. (1, 3-6, 8, 7, 11, 9, 12, 10, 13-15, 19-21, 23, 24, 2) occur in xvi.; vss. 16, 17, 37 (part) in iii.; vss. 27, 28 in viii.; vss. 24-26, 31-36 are represented by similar, but briefer and very corrupt material, in xvi.; vss. 18, 22, 37 (part), 38 are wanting тМКapparently also 29-30тМЛ. Three of the verses are quoted in V─Бit., and more in K─Бu┼Ы.: see under the verses.

Translations

Translated: Muir, v. 304-6 (parts); Ludwig, p. 435; Henry, 93, 133; Griffith, i. 442.

Griffith

A glorification of a sacrificial goat

режрез рдЖ рдирдпреИрддрдорд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Conduct him hither; take hold; let him go, foreknowing, unto the
    world of the well-doing; crossing the great darknesses variously, let
    the goat step unto the third firmament (n─Б╠Бka).
Notes

Ppp. has, in c, vipa┼Ыyaс╣Б for mah─Бnti: cf. our 3 c. The first
six verses of the hymn are quoted in their order in K─Бu┼Ы. 64. 6-16 (vs.
1 also in 64. 27) in connection with the bringing in, slaughtering, and
cooking of a goat; vss. 1 and 2 also in V─Бit. 10. 14, 15, in connection
with the sacrifice of an animal. This verse is called by the Anukr.
simply a triс╣гс╣нubh, although its first half is very irregular (8 + 13).

Griffith

Seize him and bring him hither. Let him travel. foreknowing, to the regions of the pious. Crossing in many a place the mighty darkness, let the Goat mount to the third heaven above us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I lead thee about as portion for Indra, as patron (s┼лr├н) for the
    sacrificer at this sacrifice; whoever hate us, them take hold after;
    innocent (├бn─Бgas) [are] the sacrificer’s heroes.
Notes

The verse in Ppp. (as noted above) follows what corresponds to our vs.
24, and has, for a, b, ind. bh. ┼Ыamit─Б kс╣Ыс╣Зotvaс╣Б yaj├▒a yaj├▒apati┼Ы ca
s┼лriс╕е; and, for d, ariс╣гс╣н─Б v─лr─Б yajam─Бn─Б┼Ы ca sarve.

Griffith

I bring thee hither as a share for Indra; prince, at this sacrifice,. for him who worships. Grasp firmly from behind all those who hate us: so let the sacri- ficer’s men be sinless.

режрей рдкреНрд░ рдкрджреЛрд╜рд╡ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Away from his foot wash thou down the evil walk that he walked
    (car); with cleansed hoofs let him step on, foreknowing; crossing the
    darknesses, variously looking abroad let the goat step unto the third
    firmament.
Notes

Or pad├бs in a may be accus. pl.; the redundancy of the p─Бda, in
sense and meter, is an indication of intrusion; but the mode of its
reduction to proper shape is not obvious, and Ppp. gives no help. Ppp.
has, instead of our c, d, te jyotiс╣гmantaс╣Б sukс╣Ыt─Бl lokam ─лpsan
tс╣Ыt─лye n─Бke adhi vikramasva.

Griffith

Wash from his feet all trace of evil-doing: foreknowing, with cleansed hooves let him go upward. Gazing on many a spot, crossing the darkness, let the Goat mount to the third heaven above us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Cut along this skin with the dark [metal], O slaughterer, joint by
    joint with the knife (as├н); do not plot against [him]; do not be
    hostile to [him]; prepare him joint-wise; set him up apart in the
    third firmament.
Notes

Ppp. has, for d, sukс╣Ыt─Бm madhye adhi vi ┼Ыraye тАЩmam. The Anukr.
weakly calls the verse a jagat─л, although it is a triс╣гс╣нubh with
three redundant syllables (doubtless ┼Ыy─Бm├йna or vi┼Ыastar) in a.
The pada-text divides paruре░┼Ыaс╕е, by Pr─Бt. iv. 19.

Griffith

Cut up this skin with the grey knife, Dissector! dividing joint from joint, and mangle nothing Do him no injury: limb by limb arrange him, and send him up to the third cope of heaven.

рдЕрдиреБреСред рдЪреНрдЫреНрдпреТред рд╢реНрдпрд╛реТрдореЗрдиреСред рддреНрд╡рдЪреСрдореНред рдПреТрддрд╛рдореНред рд╡рд┐реТрд╜рд╢реТрд╕реНрддрдГреТред рдпреТрдерд╛реТрд╜рдкреТрд░реБред рдЕреТрд╕рд┐рдирд╛реСред рдорд╛ред рдЕреТрднрд┐ред рдордВреТрд╕реНрдерд╛рдГреТред рдорд╛ред рдЕреТрднрд┐ред рджреНрд░реБреТрд╣рдГреТред рдкреТрд░реБреТрд╜рд╢рдГред рдХреТрд▓реНрдкреТрдпреТред рдПреТрдиреТрдореНред рддреГреТрддреАрдпреЗреСред рдирд╛рдХреЗреСред рдЕрдзрд┐реСред рд╡рд┐ред рд╢реНрд░реТрдпреТред рдПреТрдиреТрдореНред рел.рекред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╡рд┐рд╢рдиреНрддрдГ) рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рд╢рдХ ! рддреВ (рдПрддрд╛рдореН) рдЗрд╕ [рд╣реГрджрдпрд╕реНрдп] (рддреНрд╡рдЪрдореН) рдврдХрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛] рдХреЛ (рдпрдерд╛рдкрд░реБ) рдкреВрд░реНрдгрддрд╛ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рд╢реНрдпрд╛рдореЗрди) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдФрд░ (рдЕрд╕рд┐рдирд╛) рдЧрддрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЙрдкрд╛рдп рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдиреБ рдЫреНрдп) рдХрд╛рдЯ рдбрд╛рд▓, рдФрд░ (рдорд╛ рдЕрднрд┐ рдордВрд╕реНрдерд╛рдГ) рдордд рдЕрднрд┐рдорд╛рди рдХрд░ред (рдкрд░реБрд╢рдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рддреВ (рдорд╛ рдЕрднрд┐ рджреНрд░реБрд╣рдГ) рдордд рджреНрд░реЛрд╣ рдХрд░, (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕ [рдЬреАрд╡] рдХреЛ (рдХрд▓реНрдкрдп) рд╕рдорд░реНрде рдХрд░ рдФрд░ (рддреГрддреАрдпреЗ) рддреАрд╕рд░реЗ [рдЬреАрд╡ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЕрд▓рдЧ] (рдирд╛рдХреЗ) рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдореЗрдВ (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕рдХреЛ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ (рд╡рд┐ рд╢реНрд░рдп) рдлреИрд▓рдХрд░ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рджреЗ реерекрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. With a verse I set the kettle upon the fire; pour thou on the water;
    set him down; set [him] about with fire, ye quellers; when cooked, let
    him go where is the world of the well-doing.
Notes

Ppp. has instead, for a, bh┼лmy─Бс╣Б bh┼лmim adhi dh─Бray─Бmi; and, in
b, abhi for ava. The successive parts of the verse are quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 64. 11-15, to accompany corresponding acts. The Anukr. does not
heed the redundant syllable in d.

Griffith

With verse upon the fire I set the caldron: pour in the water; lay him down within it! Encompass him with fire, ye Immolators. Cooked, let him reach the world where dwell the righteous.

рдЙрддреНрдХреНрд░рд╛реТрдорд╛рддрдГреТ рдкрд░рд┐реС рдЪреЗреТрджрддреСрдкреНрддрд╕реНрддреТрдкреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдЪреТрд░реЛрд░рдзрд┐реТ рдирд╛рдХрдВреС рддреГреТрддреАрдпреСрдореНред

режрем рдЙрддреНрдХреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рддрдГ рдкрд░рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Step up from here, if thou hast been completely heated, from the
    heated pot on to the third firmament; thou, a fire, hast come into being
    out of fire; conquer [thy way] unto that world of light.
Notes

The translation of a implies the emendation to ├бtapth─Бs, which
seems very probable; nearly all the mss. read atapt─Бs (only E. ├бta-,
P.M. ataptas), which the edition has altered to ├бtaptas. Of the
reading in Ppp. I have no note; Ppp. reads for d jyotiс╣гmo acha
sukс╣Ыt─Бс╣Б yatra lokaс╕е; our d is found (nearly) as its 8 d.

Griffith

Hence come thou forth, vexed by no pain or torment. Mount to the third heaven from the heated vessel. As fire out of the fire hast thou arisen. Conquer and win this lucid world of splendour.

режрен рдЕрдЬреЛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рдЬрдореБ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The goat [is] Agni, and they call the goat light; they say that the
    goat is to be given by one living to a priest (brahm├бn); the goat,
    given in this world by one having faith, smites far away the darknesses.
Notes

For the first two words Ppp. reads ajam ev─Б тАЩgnim; in b, it puts
j─лvat─Б after brahmaс╣Зe. The redundant syllable in b is not
noticed by the Anukr. тМКSee note under 8.тМЛ

Griffith

The Goat is Agni: light they call him, saying that living man must give him to the Brahman. Given in this world by a devout believer, the Goat dispels and drives afar the darkness.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. Having five rice-dishes, let him step out five-fold, about to step
    unto the three lights; go thou forth to the midst of the well-doing that
    have made offerings; spread out (vi-┼Ыri) upon the third firmament.
Notes

The last p─Бda is the same with xviii. 4. 3 e; Ppp. has instead
jyotiс╣гmantam abhi lokaс╣Б jay─Б тАЩsm─Бi, with which compare our 6 d.
The Anukr. passes in silence the irregularities of the second p─Бda. тМКCf.

Griffith

Let the Panchaudana Goat, about to visit the three lights, pass away in five divisions. Go midst the pious who have paid their worship, and parted, dwell on the third cope of heaven.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкрдЮреНрдЪреМрджрдирдГ) рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рднреВрддреЛрдВ [рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА, рдЬрд▓, рддреЗрдЬ, рд╡рд╛рдпреБ, рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢] рд╕реЗ рд╕реАрдВрдЪрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ [рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛] (рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдзрд╛) рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ [рдЧрдиреНрдз, рд░рд╕, рд░реВрдк, рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢ рд╢рдмреНрдж рд╕реЗ] (рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐) рддреАрди [рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп] (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддреАрдВрд╖рд┐) рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ [рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЛрдВ] рдХреЛ (рдЖрдХреНрд░рдВрд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ) рдкрд╛рдиреЗ рдХреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рд╡рд┐ рдХреНрд░рдорддрд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд░рдо [рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдХрд░реЗ] (рдИрдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ [рджреЗрд╡рдкреВрдЬрд╛, рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░рдг, рджрд╛рди] рдХрд░ рдЪреБрдХрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╕реБрдХреГрддрд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдорд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдордзреНрдпрдореН) рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░) рдЖрдЧреЗ рдмрдврд╝рдХрд░ (рдЗрд╣рд┐) рдкрд╣реБрдБрдЪ, рдФрд░ (рддреГрддреАрдпреЗ) рддреАрд╕рд░реЗ [рдЬреАрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рднрд┐рдиреНрди] (рдирд╛рдХреЗ) рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ (рд╡рд┐ рд╢реНрд░рдпрд╕реНрд╡) рдлреИрд▓рдХрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдо рд▓реЗ реереорее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХреА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рднреВрддреЛрдВ рдФрд░ рдЙрдирдХреЗ рдЧрдиреНрдз рдЖрджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рд╢рд░реАрд░, рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХрд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреА рд╢рд░рдг рд▓реЗрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реереорее

режреп рдЕрдЬрд╛ рд░реЛрд╣ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Ascend, O goat, to where is the world of the well-doing; like an
    expelled ┼Ыarabh├б mayest thou move (eс╣г) across difficult places;
    given, with five rice-dishes, to a priest (brahm├бn), he shall rejoice
    the giver with rejoicing.
Notes

Ppp. reads kramasva instead of roha in a, and reads ┼Ыalabhas
’locust,’ which is more sensible, in b; our d is its 10 d,
with dh─Бt─Бram instead of d─Б-. The Anukr. treats the second p─Бda as
regular, and it can, indeed, be read by violence into 11 syllables.

Griffith

Rise to that world, O Goat, where dwell the righteous: pass, like a Sarabha veiled, all difficult places. The Goat Panchaudana, given to a Brahman, shall with all ful- ness satisfy the giver.

резреж рдЕрдЬрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдирд╛рдХреЗ рддреНрд░рд┐рджрд┐рд╡реЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The goat sets him that has given it on the three-firmamented,
    three-heavened, three-backed back of the firmament; being given with
    five rice-dishes to a priest, thou art a single milch-cow, all-formed,
    wish-yielding.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b sukс╣Ыt─Бс╣Б lake for n─Бkasya pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhe; and our d
is its 9 d, with the intrusive dhenus left out. The verse, in
spite of its irregularity, is by the Anukr. reckoned simply a jagat─л
(11 + 12: 11 + 12 [13?]).

Griffith

The Goat Panchaudana, given to a Brahman, sets the bestower on the pitch of heaven, In the third vault, third sky, third ridge. One only Cow omni- form art thou, that yields all wishes.

Whitney
Translation

11 . This third light of yours, O Fathers, the goat with five
rice-dishes one gives to a priest; the goat, given in this world by one
having faith, smites far away the darknesses.

Notes

The second half-verse is identical with 7 c, d above. Ppp. has, for
d, pa├▒codano brahmaс╣Зe d─лyam─Бnaс╕е (our 9 c, 10 c).

Griffith

That is the third light that is yours, ye Fathers. He gives the Goat Panchaudana to the Brahman. Given in this world by the devout believer, the Goat dispels and drives afar the darkness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Desiring to obtain the world of the well-doing that have made
    offerings, one gives to a priest a goat with five rice-dishes; do thou
    conquer complete attainment (vy─Б╠Аpti) unto that world; be he, accepted,
    propitious to us.
Notes

Ppp. begins pra jyotiс╣гmantaс╣Б sukс╣Ыt─Бс╣Б lok-; and reads c, d thus:
sa vy─Бpo neс╣Ес╣г abhi lokaс╣Б jay─Б тАЩsme ┼Ыivo тАШsmabhyaс╣Б pratigс╣Ыhyate тАШdhi.

Griffith

Seeking the world of good men who have worshipped, he gives the Goat Panchaudana to the Brahman. Win thou this world as thy complete possession. Auspicious unto us be he, accepted!

рдИреТрдЬрд╛реТрдирд╛рдирд╛реСрдореНред рд╕реБреТрд╜рдХреГрддрд╛реСрдореНред рд▓реЛреТрдХрдореНред рдИрдкреНрд╕реСрдиреНред рдкрдЮреНрдЪреСрд╜рдУрджрдирдореНред рдмреНрд░реТрд╣реНрдордгреЗреСред рдЕреТрдЬрдореНред рджреТрджрд╛реТрддрд┐реТред рд╕рдГред рд╡рд┐рд╜рдЖреТрдкреНрддрд┐рдореНред рдЕреТрднрд┐ред рд▓реЛреТрдХрдореНред рдЬреТрдпреТред рдПреТрддрдореНред рд╢рд┐реТрд╡рдГред рдЕреТрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпреСрдореНред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐реСрд╜рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдГред рдЕреТрд╕реНрддреБреТред рел.резреиред

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Translation
  1. A home-woven garment he may give, also gold as sacrificial gift; so

Notes
Griffith

Home-woven raiment let him give, and gold as guerdon to the priests. So he obtains completely all celestial and terrestrial worlds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unto thee, O goat, let these streams of soma (somy├б) go, divine,
    ghee-backed, honey-dripping; establish thou earth and sky, upon the
    seven-rayed back of the firmament.
Notes

The mss. in general (not P.M.) accent ├бja in a. They are rather
evenly divided between ├бdhi and тАШdhi in d (W.I.O.R.T.K. have
тАШdhi). Compare with a, b the refrain to iv. 34. 5-7. Ppp. reads
for a: et─Бs tv─Б dadh─Бr─Б тАЩcchamayanti vi┼Ыvat─Бs somyaс╣Б; тМКsomyaс╣Б
would seem to be the beginning of Ppp’s b;тМЛ in c, d, for
uta…pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhe, it gives divaс╣Б sadasva n─Бke tiс╣гс╣нh─Бsy. P─Бdas b, c
are metrically irregular, but the Anukr. does not heed it.

Griffith

Near to thee, Goat! approach these streams of Soma, divine, distilling meath, bedecked with butter! Stay thou the earth and sky and fix them firmly up on the seven- rayed pitch and height of heaven.

Convey our sacrifice to heaven, that it may reach the Gods, with that Whereby thou, Agni, bearest wealth in thousands, and all pre- cious things.

резрео рдЕрдЬрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╡рдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. The cooked goat, having five rice-dishes, driving off perdition,
    sets [one] in the heavenly (svarg├б) world; with it may we conquer
    worlds that possess suns.
Notes

As noted above, the verse is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

The Goat Panchaudana, when cooked, transporteth, repelling Nirriti, to the world of Svarga. By him may we win worlds which Surya brightens.

The droppings of the Odanas attending the Goat which I have lodged with priest or people May all this know us in the world of virtue, O Agni, at the meeting of the pathways.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The goat verily strode out here (id├бm) in the beginning; this
    [earth] became its breast, the sky its back, the atmosphere its
    middle, the quarters its (two) sides, the (two) oceans its paunches;
Notes

тМКProseтАФ20, 21, and 22.тМЛ

Griffith

This Unborn cleft apart in the beginning: his breast became the earth, his back was heaven. His middle was the air, his sides the regions; the hollows of his belly formed both oceans.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЬрдГ) рдЕрдЬрдиреНрдорд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЧрддрд┐рд╢реАрд▓ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рд╡реИ) рд╣реА (рдЕрдЧреНрд░реЗ) рдкрд╣рд┐рд▓реЗ рд╣реА рдкрд╣рд┐рд▓реЗ (рдЗрджрдореН) рдЗрд╕ [рдЬрдЧрддреН] рдореЗрдВ (рд╡рд┐ рдЕрдХреНрд░рдорддреН) рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░рддрд╛ рдерд╛, (рддрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрд╕рдХреА (рдЙрд░рдГ) рдЫрд╛рддреА (рдЗрдпрдореН) рдпрд╣ [рднреВрдорд┐] рдФрд░ (рдкреГрд╖реНрдардореН) рдкреАрда (рджреНрдпреМрдГ) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ (рдЕрднрд╡рддреН) рд╣реБрдЖред (рдордзреНрдпрдореН) рдХрдЯрд┐рднрд╛рдЧ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖, (рджрд┐рд╢рдГ) рджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдПрдБ (рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╢реНрд╡реЗ) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдХрд╛рдБрдЦреЗрдВ [рдХрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдПрдБ] рдФрд░ (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реМ) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ [рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдФрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ рдХреЗ] рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ (рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реА) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛрдЦреЗрдВ [рд╣реБрдИрдВ] реереирежрее

реирез рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЪрд░реНрддрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Both truth and right its eyes, all truth [and] faith its breath,
    the vir─Б╠Бj its head; this verily is an unlimited offering, namely
    (y├бt) the goat with five rice-dishes.
Notes

The second satyam in vs. 21 is doubtless a corrupt reading, and the
Ppp. version indicates that we should have instead r┼лp├бm (’the
universe its form,’ instead of ‘all truth’). Ppp. reads, for the two
verses: ajaс╣г pa├▒c─Бudano vy akramaia tasyo тАЩra iyam abhavad udaram
antarikс╣гam: dy─Бuс╣г с╣нe pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhaс╣Б di┼Ыaс╣г p─Бr┼Ыve: d─л┼Ыa┼Ы c─Б тАЩtid─л┼Ыa┼Ы ca ┼Ыс╣Ыn╠Дge
satyaс╣Б ca с╣Ыtaс╣Б ca cakс╣гuс╣г─л vi┼Ыvar┼лpaс╣Б ┼Ыraddh─Б etc. All the
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. read ca rt├бс╣Б (instead of ca с╣Ыt├бс╣Б) near the beginning
of vs. 21. The text of the Anukr. is apparently defective, leaving out
the metrical definition of vss. 20-22 and vs. 25.

Griffith

His eyes were Truth and Right. The whole together was Truth: Viraj his head and Faith his breathing. This Goat Panchaudana was indeed a sacrifice unlimited.

Whitney
Translation
  1. An unlimited offering does he obtain, an unlimited world does he
    take possession of (ava-rudh), who gives a goat with five rice-dishes,
    with the light of sacrificial gifts.
Notes

Wanting in Ppp., as noted above.

Griffith

A boundless sacrifice he performs, he wins himself a boundless world: Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He should not split its bones; he should not suck out its marrow;
    taking it all together, he should cause it to enter here and here.
Notes

Or, ‘should cause this and this to enter’; the sense is obscure. Ppp.
reads in c sarv─Бс╣Зi for sarvam enam. By calling the verse a
purauс╣гс╣Зih, the Anukr. intends that its first two p─Бdas be read as one,
of 12 syllables. The K─Бu┼Ы. quotes (66. 31, 32; next after quotations of
verses from hymn 3) both halves of the verse, the latter to accompany
the act of piercing an object and scattering it into a pit filled with
water.

Griffith

Let him not break the victim’s bones, let him not suck the marrow out. Let the man, taking him entire, here, even here deposit him.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This and this verily becomes its form; therewith one makes it come
    together; food, greatness, refreshment it yields (duh) to him who
    gives a goat with five rice-dishes, with the light of sacrificial gifts.
Notes

Ppp. reads for the second half-verse svadh─Бm ┼лrjam akс╣гatiс╣Б maho тАШsmai
duhe: ya evaс╣Б viduс╣гo тАШjaс╣Б pa├▒c─Бudanaс╣Б dad─Бti; and, as above noted, our
vs. 2 then follows. The metrical description of the Anukr. (closely
accordant with that of vs. 26, though the real construction of the
verses is very different) implies the artificial division of the refrain
(as in vs. 28 and other verses below) into two p─Бdas, of 7 and 9
syllables, and counts 46 syllables in all; the natural number is 45 (12

  • 8: 10 + 15 = 45).
Griffith

This, even this is his true form: the man uniteth him therewith. Food, greatness, strength he bringeth him who giveth the Goat Panchaudana illumed with guerdon.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Five gold ornaments (rukm├б), five new garments, five milch-cows
    milking his desire come to be his who gives a goat with etc. etc.
Notes

This verse, of which at least the first p─Бda is metrical (11 + 13: 15 =
39) is left undescribed in the Anukr. It (or vs. 26, both having the
same prat─лka) is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 64. 25. тМКMore nearly, ‘Five
milch-cows become wish-milking for him who,’ that is, ‘yield or grant to
him his wishes who’ etc.тМЛ

Griffith

The five gold pieces, and the five new garments, and the five milch-kine yield him all his wishes. Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Five gold ornaments become light for him; his garments become a
    defense for his body, he attains the heavenly (svarg├б) world, who
    gives a goat with etc. etc.
Notes

Here are plainly four p─Бdas, of which the first three are metrical, with
the refrain added (11 + 11: 8 + 15); the definition of the Anukr. seems
to imply 11 + 10: 8 + 7 + 9 = 45 syllables, or a bhurik triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

The five gold pieces, area light to light him, robes become armour to defend his body; He winneth Svarga as his home who giveth the Goat Panchaud- ana illumed with bountry.

Griffith

When she who hath been wedded finds a second husband after- ward, The twain shall not be parted if they give the Goat Panchaud- ana.

Translation
  1. Her later husband comes to have the same world with his remarried
    spouse who (masc.) gives a goat with five rice-dishes, with the light of
    sacrificial gifts.
Notes

The Anukr. treats the prose refrain of vss. 22, 24-26 as a half
anuс╣гс╣нubh in the second line of this verse. Ppp. reads instead ajaс╣Б ca
pa├▒c─Бudanaс╣Б dadat.

Griffith

One world with the re-wedded wife becomes the second hus- band’s home. Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with the priestly fee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever knows the season “torrid” (n─Б├нd─Бgha) by nameтАФthat verily
    is the season “torrid” by name, namely (y├бt) the goat with five
    rice-dishes; he indeed burns out the fortune of his unfriendly foe
    (bhr─Б╠Бtс╣Ыvya), he thrives (bh┼л) by himself, who gives a goat with five
    rice-dishes, with the light of sacrificial gifts.
Notes

In this and the following verses the mss. read n─Б╠Бma rt├║m etc.
throughout. The natural division is into four p─Бdas instead of seven,
and тМКthe paragraph, read as prose, hasтМЛ only 61 syllables instead of 64
(= aс╣гс╣нi); but the three missing syllables can easily be made out by
resolutions. One would expect n├н dahati, to correspond with
n─Б├нd─Бgha. Read in b y├бd aj├бс╕е (an accent-sign slipped out of
place).

Griffith

The man who knows the season named the Scorching–the Goat Pafichaudana is this scorching season He lives himself, he verily burns up his hated rival’s fame, Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with the priestly fee.

рейреи рдпреЛ рд╡реИ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever knows the season “making” by name, each making fortune of
    his unfriendly foe he takes to himself; that verily is the season
    “making” by name, namely the goat with five rice-dishes; he indeed etc.
    etc.
Notes
Griffith

The man who knows the season called the Working takes to himself the active fame, his hated rival’s active fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Working season. He lives himself, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever knows the season “gathering” by name, each gathering
    fortune of his unfriendly foe he takes to himself; that verily is the
    season “gathering” by name, namely the goat etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

The man who knows the season called the Meeting takes to him- self the gathering fame, his hated rival’s gathering fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Meeting season.

The man who knows the called the Swelling takes to himself the swelling fame, his hated rival’s swelling fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Swelling season. He lives himself, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever knows the season “up-going” by name, each up-going fortune
    of his unfriendly foe he takes to himself; that verily is the season
    “up-going” by name, namely the goat etc. etc.
Notes

These four verses agree in number of syllables, and the name given them
by the Anukr. (prakс╣Ыti) demands 84; this number it is possible to make
out by resolutions of saс╣Бdhi, though the natural reading gives only 80
(10 + 20: 15: 20 + 15 = 80). Saс╣Бyat─л╠Бmре░saс╣Бyat─лn in vs. 33 b is quoted
by the commentary under Pr─Бt. iv. 44, as an example of a repeated
separable word which gives up in pada-text its individual separation
in favor of that between the repetitions. Read in 32 c y├бd aj├бс╕е
(an accent-sign gone), and supply an omitted mark of punctuation after
datte in 33.

Griffith

The man who knows the season called the Rising takes to him- self the rising fame, his hated rival’s rising fame. The Goat Panchaudana in this Rising season.

рейрем рдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Whoever knows the season “overcoming” (abhibh┼л╠Б) by name, each
    overcoming fortune of his unfriendly foe he takes to himself; that
    verily is the season “overcoming” by name, namely the goat etc. etc.
Notes

This verse has six more syllables than the preceding ones, and the
Anukr. gives it a name (─Бkс╣Ыti) applying properly to 88 syllables. In
c read eс╣г├б for eс╣г─Б╠Б.

Griffith

The man who knows the season called Surpassing takes to him- self the conquering fame, his hated rival’s conquering fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Conquering season. He lives himself, he verily burns up his hated rival’s fame Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.

рдореВрд▓рдореН (VS)

рдЕреТрдЬрдВ рдЪреТ рдкрдЪреСрддреТ рдкрдЮреНрдЪреС рдЪреМрджреТрдирд╛рдиреНред
рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛реТ рджрд┐рд╢рдГреТ рд╕рдВрдореСрдирд╕рдГ рд╕реТрдзреНрд░реАрдЪреАрдГреТ рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддреСрд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдГреТ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐реС рдЧреГреТрд╣реНрдгрдиреНрддреБреС рдд рдПреТрддрдореН рее

рейрен рдЕрдЬрдВ рдЪ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Cook ye the goat and the five rice-dishes; let all the quarters,
    like-minded, united (sadhry├а├▒c), with the intermediate directions,
    accept that of thee.
Notes

All the mss. (except D.) read at the end t├б (pada-text t├й) before
et├бm; our edition emends to ta; the word could better be spared
altogether. Ppp. has (in iii.) only the first p─Бda. The Anukr. describes
the verse as if this p─Бda as well as the other two were metrical.

Griffith

He cooks the Goat and the five boiled rice messes. May the uni- ted Quarters, all accordant, and intermediate points, accept him from thee.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - [рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛ !] (рдЪ) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ (рдЕрдЬрдореН) рдЕрдЬрдиреНрдореЗ рд╡рд╛ рдЧрддрд┐рд╢реАрд▓ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдкрдЮреНрдЪ) рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ [рднреВрддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд] (рдУрджрдирд╛рдиреН) рд╕реЗрдЪрдХ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдкрдЪрдд) рдкрдХреНрдХрд╛ [рджреГрдврд╝] рдХрд░реЛред (рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдГ) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрджреЗрд╢реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╣рд┐рдд (рд╕рдзреНрд░реАрдЪреАрдГ) рд╕рд╛рде-рд╕рд╛рде рд░рд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА, (рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдм (рджрд┐рд╢рдГ) рджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдПрдБ (рд╕рдВрдордирд╕рдГ) рдПрдХ рдорди рд╣реЛрдХреЗ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ, (рдПрддрдореН) рдЗрд╕ [рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрдиреНрддреБ) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерейренрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let them defend this of thine for thee; to them I offer (hu)
    sacrificial butter, this oblation.
Notes

‘Them’ is fem., designating the ‘quarters’ of vs. 37. The translation
omits a te; it may be regarded as an ethical dative, anticipating the
distincter t├║bhyam ‘for thee’ that follows.

тМКThis hymn begins with ─Б╠Б naya; and, with its 38 vss., exceeds the norm
by 18. The quoted Anukr. says aс╣гс╣н─Бda┼Ы─Б тАЬтАЭnaya.тАЭтМЛ

тМКThe twentieth prap─Бс╣нhaka ends here. As in the cases of the tenth and
eighteenth (ending at v. 7 and viii. 5), the prap─Бс╣нhaka-division here
fails to coincide with the anuv─Бka-division.тМЛ

Griffith

May these preserve him for thee. Here I offer t o these the molten butter as oblation.
